```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence ‚Äî no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- taichou: physical condition, state of health
- kibun: feeling, mood
- omou: to think, to consider
- omoide: memories, recollections
- omoi: thought, imagination

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- „Çà„Åè„Å™„Å£„Åü (yokunaru): to become better [Past tense]
- „Åß„ÇÇ: even if (grammar pattern)
- „Åä„ÇÇ„ÅÑ„Åæ„Åô (omou): to think [Polite/Formal form]
- „Çè„Çã„Åè„Å¶ (warui): bad [Te-form]
- „Åü„Åπ„Çâ„Çå„Å™„Åã„Å£„Åü (taberu): to eat [Potential / Passive, Negative, Past tense]

TONE HINT:
- genkyou: present condition

Input: sensei shonichi taichou yokunatta genki aru to „Åß„ÇÇ omoimasu memai ga kibun warukute taberarenakatta
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence ‚Äî no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence ‚Äî no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- sensei: teacher, instructor
- korera: cholera
- shukudai: homework, assignment
- kudasai: please give me, please do for me
- jugyouryou: tuition fee, course fee

- „Çè„Åã„Å£„Åü (wakaru): to understand [Past tense]
- „ÅÑ„Åò„Çá„ÅÜ: so long as (grammar pattern)
- „Çè„Çãk„Å™„ÅÑ (warui): bad [Negative]
